< text>
As far a big commercial surf shops go i like this place, It still keeps its local North county vibe with staff and information, they know their boards and are more than willing to chat about a good session or what they think about products. Price wise is what you would expect, yes you can find similar items in small shops if you want to search but the one stop shop works for me if I want a new board (or just to browse and dream), or some wax. Plenty of suits, an area of used boards, and associated sundries. They also have a skate section, clothes and watches. Limited parking in the lot and on Coast Hwy, easy to find.<//text>

<Response>None< /Response>< text>
Recently opened after many years of students asking for this Seattle classic, much is still left to be desired. Manned by students (all new employees) the drinks come out slowly and many times they are not made correctly. Being the only Starbucks on a campus with 25,000 undergraduates, the line can be atrociously long. My recommendation is to go early, order black coffee and be patient. All of that said I am glad they are here on campus. Fingers crossed the baristas get better with time. Update: I went up to 4 stars today (3/22/16) because the quality of the coffee went up. Single origin dark roast freshly ground and brewed? Yes please.</text>

< Pictures>

<Date>1612999779351</Date>< Text>
I would probably drive further to another home goods store (or buy online if I'm honest) than return here. It isn't terrible - and if you live nearby and need something basic, you'll be fine - but it is not a joyful experience.
I've been in twice. The first time they didn't have what I wanted (cake pans) and the second time they had only one option (biscuit cutter). The store itself feels like an outlet store. The lighting is poor, it is very small, and lacks many choices. The final time I was in, there seemed to be an issue at each of the two open registers and the line was snaking back through the store. Unfortunately no staff member acknowledged the wait and gave us a sense of how long it might last. I get things happen - equipment fails, someone is still learning, a return is complicated - but I always appreciate someone saying "hey sorry for the wait. It should be another five or ten minutes and we really appreciate your patience," rather than ignoring the line. Both times I left without buying anything. Which reminds me that I need to go buy those cake pans and biscuit cutter!</Text>
